<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Ming_Uprising">Great Ming Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Great Ming Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A very short uprising occurred from January 25 to 28, 1903, to establish a "Great Ming Heavenly kingdom" (大明順天國).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> This involved <a href="/wiki/Tse_Tsan-tai" title="Tse Tsan-tai">Tse Tsan-tai</a>, Li Jitang (李紀堂), Liang Muguang (梁慕光) and Hong Quanfu (洪全福), who formerly took part in the <a href="/wiki/Jintian_Uprising" title="Jintian Uprising">Jintian Uprising</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Heavenly_Kingdom" title="Taiping Heavenly Kingdom">Taiping Heavenly Kingdom</a> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ping-liu-li_Uprising">Ping-liu-li Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ping-liu-li Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ma Fuyi (馬福益) and <a href="/wiki/Huaxinghui" title="Huaxinghui">Huaxinghui</a> was involved in an uprising in the three areas of <a href="/wiki/Pingxiang" title="Pingxiang">Pingxiang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liuyang" title="Liuyang">Liuyang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liling" title="Liling">Liling</a>, called "Ping-liu-li Uprising", (萍瀏醴起義) in 1905.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joan1_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joan1-47">[47]</a></sup> The uprising recruited miners as early as 1903 to rise against the Qing ruling class. After the uprising failed, Ma Fuyi was executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joan1_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Joan1-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beijing_Zhengyangmen_East_Railway_assassination_attempt">Beijing Zhengyangmen East Railway assassination attempt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Beijing Zhengyangmen East Railway assassination attempt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Wu Yue (吳樾) of <a href="/wiki/Guangfuhui" title="Guangfuhui">Guangfuhui</a> carried out an assassination attempt at the Beijing Zhengyangmen East Railway station (正陽門車站) in an attack on five Qing officials on September 24, 1905.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wangke287_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wangke287-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Huanggang_Uprising">Huanggang Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Huanggang Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Huanggang Uprising (黃岡起義) was launched on May 22, 1907, in <a href="/wiki/Chaozhou" title="Chaozhou">Chaozhou</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zga1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zga1-49">[49]</a></sup> The Revolutionary party, along with Xu Xueqiu (許雪秋), Chen Yongpo (陳湧波) and Yu Tongshi (余通實), launched the uprising and captured Huanggang city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zga1_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zga1-49">[49]</a></sup> Other Japanese that followed include (萱野長知) and (池亨吉).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zga1_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-Zga1-49">[49]</a></sup> After the uprising began, the Qing government quickly and forcefully suppressed it. Around 200 revolutionaries were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Huizhou_Qinuhu_Uprising">Huizhou Qinuhu Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Huizhou Qinuhu Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the same year, Sun Yat-sen sent more revolutionaries to <a href="/wiki/Huizhou" title="Huizhou">Huizhou</a> to launch the "Huizhou Qinuhu Uprising" (惠州七女湖起義).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zz1_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-zz1-51">[51]</a></sup> On June 2, Deng Zhiyu (鄧子瑜) and Chen Chuan (陳純) gathered some followers, and together, they seized Qing arms in the lake, 20 km (12 mi) from Huizhou.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-z3_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-z3-52">[52]</a></sup> They killed several Qing soldiers and attacked Taiwei (泰尾) on the 5th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-z3_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-z3-52">[52]</a></sup> The Qing army fled in disorder, and the revolutionaries exploited the opportunity, capturing several towns. They defeated the Qing army once again in Bazhiyie. Many organizations voiced their support after the uprising, and the number of revolutionary forces increased to two hundred men at its height. The uprising, however, ultimately failed.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="812" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg/150px-QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg/225px-QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg/300px-QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:QiuJin_feminist_revolutionary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A statue to honor revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Qiu_Jin" title="Qiu Jin">Qiu Jin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anqing_Uprising">Anqing Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Anqing Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On July 6, 1907, <a href="/wiki/Xu_Xilin" title="Xu Xilin">Xu Xilin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Guangfuhui" title="Guangfuhui">Guangfuhui</a> led an uprising in <a href="/wiki/Anqing" title="Anqing">Anqing</a>, Anhui, which became known as the Anqing Uprising (安慶起義).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mz_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-mz-25">[25]</a></sup> Xu Xilin at the time was the police commissioner as well as the supervisor of the police academy. He led an uprising that was to assassinate the provincial governor of Anhui, En Ming (恩銘).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ln1_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-ln1-53">[53]</a></sup> They were defeated after four hours of fighting. Xu was captured, and En Ming's bodyguards cut out his heart and liver and ate them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ln1_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-ln1-53">[53]</a></sup> His cousin <a href="/wiki/Qiu_Jin" title="Qiu Jin">Qiu Jin</a> was executed a few days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ln1_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-ln1-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qinzhou_Uprising">Qinzhou Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Qinzhou Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From August to September 1907, the Qinzhou Uprising occurred (欽州防城起義).,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> to protest against heavy taxation from the government. Sun Yat-sen sent Wang Heshun (王和順) there to assist the revolutionary army and captured the county in September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xn1_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-xn1-55">[55]</a></sup> After that, they attempted to besiege and capture Qinzhou, but they were unsuccessful. They eventually retreated to the area of Shiwandashan, while Wang Heshun returned to <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zhennanguan_Uprising">Zhennanguan Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Zhennanguan Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On December 1, 1907, the Zhennanguan Uprising (鎮南關起事) took place at <a href="/wiki/Friendship_Pass" title="Friendship Pass">Zhennanguan</a>, a pass on the Chinese-Vietnamese border. Sun Yat-sen sent Huang Mintang (黃明堂) to monitor the pass, which was guarded by a fort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xn1_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-xn1-55">[55]</a></sup> With the assistance of supporters among the fort's defenders, the revolutionaries captured the cannon tower in Zhennanguan. Sun Yat-sen, <a href="/wiki/Huang_Xing" title="Huang Xing">Huang Xing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hu_Hanmin" title="Hu Hanmin">Hu Hanmin</a> personally went to the tower to command the battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The Qing government sent troops led by <a href="/wiki/Long_Jiguang" title="Long Jiguang">Long Jiguang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lu_Rongting" title="Lu Rongting">Lu Rongting</a> to counterattack, and the revolutionaries were forced to retreat into the mountainous areas. After the failure of this uprising, Sun was forced to move to Singapore due to <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen#Anti-Sun_movements" title="Sun Yat-sen">anti-Sun sentiments</a> within the revolutionary groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> He would not return to the mainland until after the Wuchang Uprising.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qin-lian_Uprising">Qin-lian Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Qin-lian Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 27, 1908, Huang Xing launched a raid, later known as the Qin-lian Uprising (欽廉上思起義), from a base in Vietnam and attacked the cities of <a href="/wiki/Qinzhou" title="Qinzhou">Qinzhou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lianzhou" title="Lianzhou">Lianzhou</a> in Guangdong. The struggle continued for fourteen days but was forced to terminate after the revolutionaries ran out of supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hekou_Uprising">Hekou Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Hekou Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 1908, another uprising was launched in <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a>, Hekou, called the Hekou Uprising (雲南河口起義). Huang Mingtang (黃明堂) led two hundred men from Vietnam and attacked Hekou on April 30. Other revolutionaries who participated include Wang Heshun (王和順) and Guan Renfu (關仁甫). They were outnumbered and defeated by government troops, however, and the uprising failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mapaoying_Uprising">Mapaoying Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Mapaoying Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 19, 1908, the Mapaoying Uprising (馬炮營起義) was launched by revolutionary group Yuewanghui (岳王會) member Xiong Chenggei (熊成基) at <a href="/wiki/Anhui" title="Anhui">Anhui</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Yuewanghui, at this time, was a subset of <a href="/wiki/Tongmenghui" title="Tongmenghui">Tongmenghui</a>. This uprising also failed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gengxu_New_Army_Uprising">Gengxu New Army Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Gengxu New Army Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 1910, the Gengxu New Army Uprising (庚戌新軍起義), also known as the Guangzhou New Army Uprising (廣州新軍起義), took place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yq_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-yq-61">[61]</a></sup> This involved a conflict between the citizens and local police against the New Army. After revolutionary leader Ni Yingdian was killed by Qing forces, the remaining revolutionaries were quickly defeated, causing the uprising to fail.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg/220px-Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg/330px-Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg/440px-Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Huanghuagang_Mausoleum_of_72_Martyrs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The memorial for the 72 martyrs</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Guangzhou_Uprising">Second Guangzhou Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Second Guangzhou Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Guangzhou_Uprising" title="Second Guangzhou Uprising">Second Guangzhou Uprising</a></div>
<p>On April 27, 1911, an uprising occurred in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, known as the Second Guangzhou Uprising (辛亥廣州起義) or Yellow Flower Mound Revolt (黃花岡之役). It ended in disaster, as only 72 bodies were ever found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gongtong1_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-gongtong1-62">[62]</a></sup> The 72 revolutionaries were remembered as <a href="/wiki/Martyrdom_in_Chinese_culture" title="Martyrdom in Chinese culture">martyrs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gongtong1_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-gongtong1-62">[62]</a></sup> Revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Lin_Juemin" title="Lin Juemin">Lin Juemin</a> (林覺民) was one of the 72. On the eve of battle, he wrote the legendary "A Letter to My Wife" (與妻訣別書), later to be considered as a masterpiece in Chinese literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langmead_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Langmead-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wuchang_Uprising">Wuchang Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Wuchang Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_(1911-1928)_18_dots.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="780" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_%281911-1928%29_18_dots.svg/200px-Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_%281911-1928%29_18_dots.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_%281911-1928%29_18_dots.svg/300px-Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_%281911-1928%29_18_dots.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_%281911-1928%29_18_dots.svg/400px-Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_%281911-1928%29_18_dots.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chinese-army_Wuhan_flag_(1911-1928)_18_dots.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Iron blood 18-star flag</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1178" data-file-width="634" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png/100px-%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png/150px-%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png/200px-%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png 2x" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E6%AD%A6%E6%98%8C%E8%B5%B7%E4%B9%89.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paths of the uprising</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wuchang_Uprising" title="Wuchang Uprising">Wuchang Uprising</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yangxia" title="Battle of Yangxia">Battle of Yangxia</a></div>
<p>The Literary Society (文學社) and the Progressive Association (共進會) were revolutionary organizations involved in the uprising that mainly began with a <a href="/wiki/Railway_Protection_Movement" title="Railway Protection Movement">Railway Protection Movement</a> protest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang390_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wang390-24">[24]</a></sup> In the late summer, some Hubei New Army units were ordered to neighboring Sichuan to quell the Railway Protection Movement, a mass protest against the Qing government's seizure and handover of local railway development ventures to foreign powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reillyt_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-reillyt-64">[64]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eight_Banner" title="Eight Banner">Banner</a> officers like <a href="/wiki/Duanfang" title="Duanfang">Duanfang</a>, the railroad superintendent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Erfeng" title="Zhao Erfeng">Zhao Erfeng</a> led the New Army against the Railway Protection Movement.</p>
<p>The New Army units of Hubei had originally been the Hubei Army, which had been trained by Qing official <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Zhidong" title="Zhang Zhidong">Zhang Zhidong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xb1_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-xb1-2">[2]</a></sup> On September 24, the Literary Society and Progressive Association convened a conference in Wuchang, along with sixty representatives from local New Army units. During the conference, they established a headquarters for the uprising. The leaders of the two organizations, Jiang Yiwu (蔣翊武) and Sun Wu (孫武), were elected as commander and chief of staff. Initially, the date of the uprising was to be October 6, 1911.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gongtong2_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-gongtong2-66">[66]</a></sup> It was postponed to a later date due to insufficient preparations.</p>
<p>Revolutionaries intent on overthrowing the Qing dynasty had built bombs, and on October 9, one accidentally exploded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gongtong2_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-gongtong2-66">[66]</a></sup> Sun Yat-sen himself had no direct part in the uprising and was traveling in the United States at the time in an effort to recruit more support from among overseas Chinese. The Qing <a href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_Huguang" title="Viceroy of Huguang">Viceroy of Huguang</a>, Rui Cheng (瑞澂), tried to track down and arrest the revolutionaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tonsi1_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-tonsi1-67">[67]</a></sup> Squad leader Xiong Bingkun (熊秉坤) and others decided not to delay the uprising any longer and launched the revolt on October 10, 1911, at 7 pm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tonsi1_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-tonsi1-67">[67]</a></sup> The revolt was a success; the entire city of Wuchang was captured by the revolutionaries on the morning of October 11. That evening, they established a tactical headquarters and announced the establishment of the "Military Government of Hubei of Republic of China".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tonsi1_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-tonsi1-67">[67]</a></sup> The conference chose <a href="/wiki/Li_Yuanhong" title="Li Yuanhong">Li Yuanhong</a> as the governor of the temporary government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tonsi1_67-3"><a href="#cite_note-tonsi1-67">[67]</a></sup> Qing officers like the bannermen Duanfang and Zhao Erfeng were killed by the revolutionary forces.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Provincial_Uprisings">Provincial Uprisings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Provincial Uprisings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9200" data-file-width="6400" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG/200px-Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG/300px-Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG/400px-Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qing_Dynasty_Map_durnig_Xinhai_Revolution.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Uprising map during the Xinhai Revolution</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the success of the Wuchang Uprising, many other protests occurred throughout the country for various reasons. Some of the uprisings restored imperial rule (光復). Other uprisings were a step toward independence, and some were protests or rebellions against the local authorities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Regardless the reason for the uprising the outcome was that all provinces in the country renounced the Qing dynasty and joined the ROC.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Changsha_restoration">Changsha restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Changsha restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Changsha_(1911)" title="Battle of Changsha (1911)">Battle of Changsha (1911)</a></div>
<p>On October 22, 1911, the <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a> Tongmenghui were led by Jiao Dafeng (焦達嶧) and Chen Zuoxin (陳作新).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhanged2_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-zhanged2-68">[68]</a></sup> They headed an armed group, consisting partly of revolutionaries from <a href="/wiki/Hongjiang" title="Hongjiang">Hongjiang</a> and partly of defecting New Army units, in a campaign to extend the uprising into <a href="/wiki/Changsha" title="Changsha">Changsha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhanged2_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-zhanged2-68">[68]</a></sup> They captured the city and killed the local Imperial general. Then they announced the establishment of the Hunan Military Government of the Republic of China and announced their opposition to the Qing Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhanged2_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-zhanged2-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shaanxi_Uprising">Shaanxi Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Shaanxi Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the same day, <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a>'s Tongmenghui, led by Jing Dingcheng (景定成) and Qian ding (錢鼎) as well as Jing Wumu (井勿幕) and others including <a href="/wiki/Gelaohui" title="Gelaohui">Gelaohui</a>, launched an uprising and captured <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi'an">Xi'an</a> after two days of struggle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Muslim" title="Chinese Muslim">Muslim</a> general <a href="/wiki/Ma_Anliang" title="Ma Anliang">Ma Anliang</a> led more than twenty battalions of <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Hui</a> Muslim troops to defend the Qing imperials and attacked Shaanxi, held by revolutionary Zhang Fenghui (張鳳翽).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fsh_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-fsh-70">[70]</a></sup> The attack was successful, but after news arrived that Puyi was about to abdicate, Ma agreed to join the new Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fsh_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-fsh-70">[70]</a></sup> The revolutionaries established the "Qinlong Fuhan Military Government" and elected Zhang Fenghui, a member of the Yuanrizhi Society (原日知會), as new governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> Xi'an Manchu city (滿城) finally fell on October 24, after a massacre of its Manchu residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads192_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads192-71">[71]</a></sup> Many of its Manchu defenders committed suicide, including Qing general Wenrui (文瑞), who threw himself down a well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads192_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads192-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jiujiang_Uprising">Jiujiang Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Jiujiang Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 23, <a href="/wiki/Lin_Sen" title="Lin Sen">Lin Sen</a>, Jiang Qun (蔣群), Cai Hui (蔡蕙) and other members of the Tongmenghui in the province of <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a> plotted a revolt of New Army units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhanged2_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-zhanged2-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> After they achieved victory, they announced their independence. The Jiujiang Military Government was then established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shanxi_Taiyuan_Uprising">Shanxi Taiyuan Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Shanxi Taiyuan Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 29, <a href="/wiki/Yan_Xishan" title="Yan Xishan">Yan Xishan</a> of the New Army led an uprising in <a href="/wiki/Taiyuan" title="Taiyuan">Taiyuan</a>, the capital city of the province of <a href="/wiki/Shanxi" title="Shanxi">Shanxi</a>, along with Yao Yijie (姚以價), Huang Guoliang (黃國梁), Wen Shouquan (溫壽泉), Li Chenglin (李成林), Zhang Shuzhi (張樹幟) and Qiao Xi (喬煦).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> They managed to kill the Qing Governor of Shanxi, Lu Zhongqi (陸鍾琦).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> They then announced the establishment of Shanxi Military Government with Yan Xishan as the military governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> Yan Xishan would later become one of the warlords that plagued China during what was known as "the warlord era".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kunming_Double_Ninth_Uprising">Kunming Double Ninth Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Kunming Double Ninth Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 30, Li Genyuan (李根源) of the Tongmenghui in <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a> province joined with <a href="/wiki/Cai_E" title="Cai E">Cai E</a>, Luo Peijin (羅佩金), <a href="/wiki/Tang_Jiyao" title="Tang Jiyao">Tang Jiyao</a>, and other officers of the New Army to launch the <a href="/wiki/Double_Ninth_Festival" title="Double Ninth Festival">Double Ninth</a> Uprising (重九起義).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> They captured <a href="/wiki/Kunming" title="Kunming">Kunming</a> the next day and established the Yunnan Military Government, electing <a href="/wiki/Cai_E" title="Cai E">Cai E</a> as the military governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-3"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nanchang_restoration">Nanchang restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Nanchang restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 31, the <a href="/wiki/Nanchang" title="Nanchang">Nanchang</a> branch of the Tongmenghui led New Army units in a successful uprising. They established the Jiangxi Military Government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhanged2_68-4"><a href="#cite_note-zhanged2-68">[68]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Li_Liejun" title="Li Liejun">Li Liejun</a> was elected as the military governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-4"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> Li declared <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a> as independent and launched an expedition against Qing official Yuan Shikai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langmead_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Langmead-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chen_Qi-mei.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="735" data-file-width="558" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Chen_Qi-mei.png/150px-Chen_Qi-mei.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Chen_Qi-mei.png/225px-Chen_Qi-mei.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Chen_Qi-mei.png/300px-Chen_Qi-mei.png 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chen_Qi-mei.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Chen_Qimei" title="Chen Qimei">Chen Qimei</a>, military governor of Shanghai</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shanghai_Armed_Uprising">Shanghai Armed Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Shanghai Armed Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 3, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>'s Tongmenghui, Guangfuhui and merchants led by <a href="/wiki/Chen_Qimei" title="Chen Qimei">Chen Qimei</a> (陳其美), Li Pingsu (李平書), Zhang Chengyou (張承槱), Li Yingshi (李英石), Li Xiehe (李燮和) and <a href="/wiki/Song_Jiaoren" title="Song Jiaoren">Song Jiaoren</a> organized an armed rebellion in Shanghai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-5"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> They received the support of local police officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-6"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> The rebels captured the Jiangnan Workshop on the 4th and captured Shanghai soon after. On November 8, they established the Shanghai Military Government and elected Chen Qimei as the military governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-7"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> He would eventually become one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Four_big_families_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Four big families of the Republic of China">ROC four big families</a>, along with some of the most well-known families of the era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guizhou_Uprising">Guizhou Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Guizhou Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 4, Zhang Bailin (張百麟) of the revolutionary party in <a href="/wiki/Guizhou" title="Guizhou">Guizhou</a> led an uprising along with New Army units and students from the military academy. They immediately captured <a href="/wiki/Guiyang" title="Guiyang">Guiyang</a> and established the Great Han Guizhou Military Government, electing Yang Jincheng (楊藎誠) and Zhao Dequan (趙德全) as the chief and vice governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zhejiang_Uprising">Zhejiang Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Zhejiang Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Also on November 4, revolutionaries in <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a> urged the New Army units in <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a> to launch an uprising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-8"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> Zhu Rui (朱瑞), Wu Siyu (吳思豫), Lu Gongwang (吕公望) and others of the New Army captured the military supplies workshop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-9"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> Other units, led by <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> and Yin Zhirei (尹銳志), captured most of the government offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-10"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup> Eventually, Hangzhou was under the control of the revolutionaries, and the constitutionist Tang Shouqian (湯壽潛) was elected as the military governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-11"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jiangsu_restoration">Jiangsu restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Jiangsu restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 5, <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> constitutionists and gentry urged Qing governor Cheng Dequan (程德全) to announce independence and established the Jiangsu Revolutionary Military Government with Cheng himself as the governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhong1911-ch12_72-12"><a href="#cite_note-zhong1911-ch12-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Unlike some of the other cities, anti-Manchu violence began after the restoration on November 7 in <a href="/wiki/Zhenjiang" title="Zhenjiang">Zhenjiang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads194_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads194-79">[79]</a></sup> Qing general Zaimu (載穆) agreed to surrender, but because of a misunderstanding, the revolutionaries were unaware that their safety was guaranteed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads194_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads194-79">[79]</a></sup> The Manchu quarters were ransacked, and an unknown number of Manchus were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads194_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads194-79">[79]</a></sup> Zaimu, feeling betrayed, committed suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads194_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads194-79">[79]</a></sup> This is regarded as the Zhenjiang Uprising (鎮江起義).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anhui_Uprising">Anhui Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Anhui Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Members of <a href="/wiki/Anhui" title="Anhui">Anhui</a>'s Tongmenghui also launched an uprising on that day and laid siege to the provincial capital. The constitutionists persuaded Zhu Jiabao (朱家寶), the Qing Governor of Anhui, to announce independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guangxi_Uprising">Guangxi Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Guangxi Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 7, the <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a> politics department decided to secede from the Qing government, announcing Guangxi's independence. Qing Governor Shen Bingkun (沈秉堃) was allowed to remain governor, but <a href="/wiki/Lu_Rongting" title="Lu Rongting">Lu Rongting</a> would soon become the new governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xn1_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-xn1-55">[55]</a></sup> Lu Rongting would later rise to prominence during the "warlord era" as one of the warlods, and his bandits controlled Guangxi for more than a decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Huang_Shaohong" title="Huang Shaohong">Huang Shaohong</a>, the Muslim law student <a href="/wiki/Bai_Chongxi" title="Bai Chongxi">Bai Chongxi</a> enlisted in a Dare to Die unit to fight as a revolutionary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoormanHoward1967_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoormanHoward1967-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="406" data-file-width="554" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg/220px-%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg/330px-%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg/440px-%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E8%BF%9E%E6%B1%9F%E5%85%89%E5%A4%8D%E4%BC%9A%E6%97%A7%E5%9D%80.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the old <a href="/wiki/Guangfuhui" title="Guangfuhui">Guangfuhui</a> addressing in <a href="/wiki/Lianjiang_County" title="Lianjiang County">Lianjiang County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fujian_independence">Fujian independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Fujian independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November, members of <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>'s branch of the Tongmenghui, along with Sun Daoren (孫道仁) of the New Army, launched an uprising against the Qing army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gli_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-gli-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The Qing viceroy, Song Shou (松壽), committed suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On November 11, the entire Fujian province declared independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gli_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-gli-85">[85]</a></sup> The Fujian Military Government was established, and Sun Daoren was elected as the military governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gli_85-2"><a href="#cite_note-gli-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guangdong_independence">Guangdong independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Guangdong independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Near the end of October, <a href="/wiki/Chen_Jiongming" title="Chen Jiongming">Chen Jiongming</a>, Deng Keng (鄧鏗), Peng Reihai (彭瑞海) and other members of Guangdong's Tongmenghui organized local militias to launch the uprising in <a href="/wiki/Huazhou,_Guangdong" title="Huazhou, Guangdong">Huazhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanhai_District" title="Nanhai District">Nanhai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shunde_District" title="Shunde District">Sunde</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanshui_District" title="Sanshui District">Sanshui</a> in Guangdong Province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> On November 8, after being persuaded by <a href="/wiki/Hu_Hanmin" title="Hu Hanmin">Hu Hanmin</a>, General Li Zhun (李準) and Long Jiguang (龍濟光) of the Guangdong Navy agreed to support the revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-4"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> The Qing <a href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_Liangguang" title="Viceroy of Liangguang">viceroy of Liangguang</a>, Zhang Mingqi (張鳴岐), was forced to discuss with the local representatives a proposal for Guangdong's independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-5"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> They decided to announce it the next day. Chen Jiongming then captured <a href="/wiki/Huizhou" title="Huizhou">Huizhou</a>. On November 9, Guangdong announced its independence and established a military government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qiuf_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-qiuf-89">[89]</a></sup> They elected Hu Hanmin and Chen Jiongming as the chief and vice governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Qiu_Fengjia" title="Qiu Fengjia">Qiu Fengjia</a> is known to have helped make the independence declaration more peaceful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qiuf_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-qiuf-89">[89]</a></sup> It was unknown if representatives from the European colonies of <a href="/wiki/British_Hong_Kong" title="British Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Macau</a> will be ceded to the new government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shandong_independence">Shandong independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Shandong independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 13, persuaded by revolutionary Din Weifen (丁惟汾) and several other officers of the New Army, the Qing governor of <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Baoqi" title="Sun Baoqi">Sun Baoqi</a>, agreed to secede from the Qing government and announced Shandong's independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-6"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ningxia_Uprising">Ningxia Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Ningxia Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 17, <a href="/wiki/Ningxia" title="Ningxia">Ningxia</a> the Tongmenghui launched the Ningxia Uprising (寧夏會黨起義). The revolutionaries sent <a href="/wiki/Yu_Youren" title="Yu Youren">Yu Youren</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhangjiachuan_County" title="Zhangjiachuan County">Zhangjiachuan</a> to meet <a href="/wiki/Dungan_people" title="Dungan people">Dungan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> master <a href="/wiki/Ma_Yuanzhang" title="Ma Yuanzhang">Ma Yuanzhang</a> to persuade him not to support the Qing. However, Ma did not want to endanger his relationship with the Qings. He sent the eastern <a href="/wiki/Gansu" title="Gansu">Gansu</a> Muslim militia under the command of one of his sons to help <a href="/wiki/Ma_Qi" title="Ma Qi">Ma Qi</a> crush the Ningxia Gelaohui.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUP_Archive_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-CUP_Archive-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The Ningxia Revolutionary Military Government was established on November 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-7"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> Some of the revolutionaries involved included Huang Yue (黃鉞) and Xiang Shen (向燊), who gathered New Army forces at Qinzhou (秦州).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sichuan_independence">Sichuan independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Sichuan independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 21, <a href="/wiki/Guang%27an" title="Guang'an">Guang'an</a> organized the Great Han <a href="/wiki/Shu_Han" title="Shu Han">Shu</a> northern Military Government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-8"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 22, <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> began to declare independence. By the 27th, the Great Han Sichuan Military Government was established, headed by revolutionary Pu Dianzun (蒲殿俊).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-9"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> Qing official <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duan_Fang" title="Duan Fang">Duan Fang</a> (端方) would also be killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-10"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nanking_Uprising">Nanking Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Nanking Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China,_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5106" data-file-width="7087" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China%2C_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg/220px-An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China%2C_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China%2C_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg/330px-An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China%2C_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China%2C_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg/440px-An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China%2C_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:An_episode_in_the_revolutionary_war_in_China,_1911_-_the_battle_at_the_Ta-ping_gate_at_Nanking._Wellcome_L0040002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1911 battle at Ta-ping gate, Nanking. Painting by T. Miyano.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On November 8, supported by the Tongmenghui, Xu Shaozhen (徐紹楨) of the New Army announced an uprising in Molin Pass (秣陵關), 30 km (19 mi) away from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_City" title="Nanjing City">Nanking City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-11"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> Xu Shaozhen, Chen Qimei and other generals decided to form a united army under Xu to strike Nanking together. On November 11, the united army headquarters was established in Zhenjiang. Between November 24 and December 1, under the command of Xu Shaozhen, the united army captured Wulongshan (烏龍山), Mufushan (幕府山), Yuhuatai (雨花臺), Tianbao City (天保城) and many other strongholds of the Qing army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-12"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> On December 2, Nanking City was captured by the revolutionaries after the Battle of Nanking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigxz13_69-13"><a href="#cite_note-bigxz13-69">[69]</a></sup> On December 3, revolutionary Su Liangbi led troops in a massacre of a large number of Manchus (the exact number is not known).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads198_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads198-96">[96]</a></sup> He was shortly afterward arrested, and his troops disbanded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads198_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads198-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tibetan_independence">Tibetan independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Tibetan independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinhai_Lhasa_Turmoil" title="Xinhai Lhasa Turmoil">Xinhai Lhasa Turmoil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibet_(1912%E2%80%9351)" title="Tibet (1912–51)">Tibet (1912–51)</a></div>
<p>In 1905, the Qing sent <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Erfeng" title="Zhao Erfeng">Zhao Erfeng</a> to Tibet to retaliate against <a href="/wiki/1905_Tibetan_Rebellion" title="1905 Tibetan Rebellion">rebellions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blondeau_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blondeau-97">[97]</a></sup> By 1908, Zhao was appointed <a href="/wiki/List_of_Qing_imperial_residents_in_Tibet" title="List of Qing imperial residents in Tibet">imperial resident</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blondeau_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Blondeau-97">[97]</a></sup> Zhao was beheaded in December 1911 by pro-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Republican</a> forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The bulk of the area that was historically known as <a href="/wiki/Kham" title="Kham">Kham</a> was now the <a href="/wiki/Xikang" title="Xikang">Xikang Administrative District</a>, created by the Republican revolutionaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> By the end of 1912, the last Manchu troops were escorted out of Tibet. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thubten_Gyatso" title="Thubten Gyatso">Thubten Gyatso</a>, the 13th <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a>, returned to Tibet in January 1913 from <a href="/wiki/Sikkim" title="Sikkim">Sikkim</a>, where he had been residing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mayhew_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mayhew-100">[100]</a></sup> When the new ROC government apologised for the actions of the Qing and offered to restore the Dalai Lama to his former position, he replied that he was not interested in Chinese ranks, that Tibet had never been subordinated to China, that Tibet was an independent country, and that he was assuming the spiritual and political leadership of Tibet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mayhew_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mayhew-100">[100]</a></sup> Because of this, many have read this reply as a formal declaration of independence. The Chinese side ignored the response, and Tibet had thirty years free of interference from China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mayhew_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mayhew-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mongolian_independence">Mongolian independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Mongolian independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Revolution_of_1911" title="Mongolian Revolution of 1911">Mongolian Revolution of 1911</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outer_Mongolia_(1911%E2%80%9319)" title="Outer Mongolia (1911–19)">Outer Mongolia (1911–19)</a></div>
<p>At the end of 1911, the Mongols took action with an armed revolt against the Manchu authorities but were unsuccessful in the attempt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Onon_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Onon-101">[101]</a></sup> An independence movement took place that was not limited to just North (outer) Mongolia but was a pan-Mongolian phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Onon_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Onon-101">[101]</a></sup> On December 29, 1911, <a href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan" title="Bogd Khan">Bogd Khan</a> became the leader of the Mongol empire. <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a> became a contested terrain between Khan and the Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In general, Russia supported the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outer_Mongolian_revolution_of_1911" title="Outer Mongolian revolution of 1911">Independence of Outer Mongolia</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Tannu_Uriankhai" title="Tannu Uriankhai">Tannu Uriankhai</a>) during the time of the Xinhai Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Tibet and Mongolia then recognized each other in a treaty.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dihua_and_Yili_Uprising">Dihua and Yili Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Dihua and Yili Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Xinjiang" title="Xinhai Revolution in Xinjiang">Xinhai Revolution in Xinjiang</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> on December 28, Liu Xianzun (劉先俊) and the revolutionaries started the <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi" title="Ürümqi">Dihua</a> Uprising (迪化起義).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doizung_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-doizung-104">[104]</a></sup> This was led by more than 100 members of Geilaohui.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hkcna_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-hkcna-105">[105]</a></sup> This uprising failed. On January 7, 1912, the <a href="/wiki/Ili_Kazakh_Autonomous_Prefecture" title="Ili Kazakh Autonomous Prefecture">Yili</a> Uprising (伊犁起義) with Feng Temin (馮特民) began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doizung_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-doizung-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hkcna_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-hkcna-105">[105]</a></sup> Qing governor Yuan Dahua (袁大化) fled and handed over his resignation to <a href="/wiki/Yang_Zengxin" title="Yang Zengxin">Yang Zengxin</a>, because he could not handle fighting the revolutionaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yz_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-yz-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the morning of January 8, a new Yili government was established for the revolutionaries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hkcna_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-hkcna-105">[105]</a></sup> but the revolutionaries would be defeated at <a href="/wiki/Jinghe_County" title="Jinghe County">Jinghe</a> in January and February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yz_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-yz-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wamu_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-wamu-107">[107]</a></sup> Eventually because of the abdication to come, Yuan Shikai recognized Yang Zengxin's rule, appointed him Governor of Xinjiang and had the province join the Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yz_106-2"><a href="#cite_note-yz-106">[106]</a></sup> Eleven more former Qing officials would be assassinated in <a href="/wiki/Bark%C3%B6l_Kazakh_Autonomous_County" title="Barköl Kazakh Autonomous County">Zhenxi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karashahr" title="Karashahr">Karashahr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aksu,_Xinjiang" title="Aksu, Xinjiang">Aksu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kucha" title="Kucha">Kucha</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luntai" title="Luntai">Luntai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashgar</a> in April and May 1912.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yz_106-3"><a href="#cite_note-yz-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>The revolutionaries printed new multi-lingual media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan_Uprising">Taiwan Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Taiwan Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1911 as part of the Xinhai Revolution, Tongmenghui sent Luo Fu-xing (羅福星) to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_island" title="Taiwan island">island of Taiwan</a> to free it from being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_rule_in_Taiwan" title="Japanese rule in Taiwan">occupied by the Japanese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The goal was to bring Taiwan island back to the Chinese Republic by having the Taiwan Uprising (台灣起義).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Luo was caught and killed on March 3, 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dellorto_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dellorto-111">[111]</a></sup> What was left was known as the "<a href="/wiki/Miaoli_County" title="Miaoli County">Miaoli</a> incident", (苗栗事件) where more than 1,000 Taiwanese were executed by the Japanese police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Luo's sacrifice is commemorated in Miaoli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dellorto_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dellorto-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Change_of_government">Change of government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Change of government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North:_Qing_court_last_transformation_attempt">North: Qing court last transformation attempt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: North: Qing court last transformation attempt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 1, 1911, the Qing government appointed Yuan Shikai as the prime minister of the imperial cabinet, replacing <a href="/wiki/Yikuang,_Prince_Qing" title="Yikuang, Prince Qing">Prince Qing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> On November 3, after a proposition by <a href="/wiki/Cen_Chunxuan" title="Cen Chunxuan">Cen Chunxuan</a> from the Constitutional Monarchy Movement (立憲運動), in 1903, the Qing court passed the Nineteen Articles (憲法重大信條十九條), which turned the Qing from an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autocratic" title="Autocratic">autocratic</a> system with the emperor having unlimited power to a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhoads228_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rhoads228-115">[115]</a></sup> On November 9, <a href="/wiki/Huang_Xing" title="Huang Xing">Huang Xing</a> even cabled Yuan Shikai and invited him to join the Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pompl_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-pompl-116">[116]</a></sup> The court changes were too late, and the emperor was about to have to step down.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South:_Government_in_Nanking">South: Government in Nanking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: South: Government in Nanking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_the_Republic_of_China_(1912)" title="Provisional Government of the Republic of China (1912)">Provisional Government of the Republic of China (1912)</a></div>
<p>On November 28, 1911, Wuchang and <a href="/wiki/Hanyang_District" title="Hanyang District">Hanyang</a> had fallen back to the Qing army. So for safety, the revolutionaries convened their first conference at the British concession in <a href="/wiki/Hankou" title="Hankou">Hankou</a> on November 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ksliew_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-ksliew-117">[117]</a></sup> By December 2, the revolutionary forces were able to <a href="#Nanking_Uprising">capture Nanking in the uprising</a>; the revolutionaries decided to make it the site of the new provisional government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> At the time, Beijing was still the Qing capital.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanbeihetan_1911.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="171" data-file-width="227" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Nanbeihetan_1911.png/220px-Nanbeihetan_1911.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Nanbeihetan_1911.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North-South_Conference">North-South Conference</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: North-South Conference">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On December 18, the North-South Conference (南北議和) was held in Shanghai to discuss the north and south issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liwanhon_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-liwanhon-119">[119]</a></sup> Yuan Shikai selected <a href="/wiki/Tang_Shaoyi" title="Tang Shaoyi">Tang Shaoyi</a> as his representative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liwanhon_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-liwanhon-119">[119]</a></sup> Tang left Beijing for Wuhan to negotiate with the revolutionaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liwanhon_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-liwanhon-119">[119]</a></sup> The revolutionaries chose <a href="/wiki/Wu_Tingfang" title="Wu Tingfang">Wu Tingfang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liwanhon_119-3"><a href="#cite_note-liwanhon-119">[119]</a></sup> With the intervention of six foreign powers, the United Kingdom, the United States, Germany, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a>, Japan, and France, Tang Shaoyi and Wu Tingfang began to negotiate a settlement at the British <a href="/wiki/Concession_(territory)" title="Concession (territory)">concession</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Foreign businessman Edward Selby Little (李德立) acted as the negotiator and facilitated the peace agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> They agreed that Yuan Shikai would force the Qing emperor to abdicate in exchange for the southern provinces' support of Yuan as the president of the Republic. After considering the possibility that the new republic might be defeated in a civil war or by foreign invasion, Sun Yat-sen agreed to Yuan's proposal to unify China under Yuan Shikai's Beijing government. Further decisions were made to let the emperor rule over his little court in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Summer_Palace" title="New Summer Palace">New Summer Palace</a>. He would be treated as a ruler of a separate country and have expenses of several million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taels" title="Taels">taels</a> in silver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_of_the_Republic">Establishment of the Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Establishment of the Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1912Jimingxiaoling2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="769" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/1912Jimingxiaoling2.jpg/220px-1912Jimingxiaoling2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/1912Jimingxiaoling2.jpg/330px-1912Jimingxiaoling2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/1912Jimingxiaoling2.jpg/440px-1912Jimingxiaoling2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_China_declared_and_national_flag_issue">Republic of China declared and national flag issue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Republic of China declared and national flag issue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_provisional_presidential_election,_1911" title="Republic of China provisional presidential election, 1911">On December 29, 1911, Sun Yat-sen was elected</a> as the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_leaders_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="List of leaders of the Republic of China">provisional president</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> January 1, 1912, was set as the <a href="/wiki/Epoch_(reference_date)" title="Epoch (reference date)">first day</a> of the First Year of the ROC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Well_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Well-124">[124]</a></sup> On January 3, the representatives recommended Li Yuanhong as the provisional vice president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>During and after the Xinhai Revolution, many groups that participated wanted their own pennant as the national flag. During the Wuchang Uprising, the military units of Wuchang wanted the nine-star flag with <a href="/wiki/Taijitu" title="Taijitu">Taijitu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitzj_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-fitzj-126">[126]</a></sup> Others in competition included <a href="/wiki/Lu_Haodong" title="Lu Haodong">Lu Haodong</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Blue_Sky_with_a_White_Sun" title="Blue Sky with a White Sun">Blue Sky with a White Sun</a> flag. <a href="/wiki/Huang_Xing" title="Huang Xing">Huang Xing</a> favored a flag bearing the mythical "well-field" system of village agriculture. In the end, the assembly compromised: the national flag would be the banner of <a href="/wiki/Five_Races_Under_One_Union" title="Five Races Under One Union">Five Races Under One Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitzj_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-fitzj-126">[126]</a></sup> The Five Races Under One Union flag with horizontal stripes represented the five major nationalities of the republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newlight10-92_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-newlight10-92-127">[127]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">red</a> represented <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han</a>, the yellow represented <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">blue</a> for <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a>, the white for <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">Muslims</a>, and the black for <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_people" title="Tibetan people">Tibetans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitzj_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-fitzj-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newlight10-92_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-newlight10-92-127">[127]</a></sup> Despite the general target of the uprisings to be the Manchus, Sun Yat-sen, Song Jiaoren and Huang Xing unanimously advocated <a href="/wiki/Racial_integration" title="Racial integration">racial integration</a> to be carried out from the mainland to the frontiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Donghuamen_incident">Donghuamen incident</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhai_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Donghuamen incident">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 16, while returning to his residence, Yuan Shikai was ambushed in a bomb attack organized by the Tongmenghui in Donghuamen (東華門), <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tientsin</a>, Beijing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-gg-129">[129]</a></sup> A total of eighteen revolutionaries were involved. About ten of the guards died, but Yuan himself was not seriously injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-gg-129">[129]</a></sup> He sent a message to the revolutionaries the next day pledging his loyalty and asking them not to organize any more assassination attempts against him.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qingtuiweizhaoshu.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="565" data-file-width="1424" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Qingtuiweizhaoshu.JPG/300px-Qingtuiweizhaoshu.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Qingtuiweizhaoshu.JPG/450px-Qingtuiweizhaoshu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Qingtuiweizhaoshu.JPG/600px-Qingtuiweizhaoshu.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a>

Imperial edict for abdication</div>
